Miracles
intermediate
6 min
The Skeptical Objection to Miracles
Skeptic denies miracles and argues they could be natural or magical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key arguments used by skeptics to deny that miracles prove prophethood, including the denial of reported miracles, the possibility of natural or magical explanations, and the critique of a miracle's indication of truth.

Core Idea
Extraordinary events alone do not automatically prove a prophet's truthfulness.

Before we can affirm the role of miracles in establishing prophethood, we must first confront a powerful skeptical challenge. This passage presents that challenge in its full force: it denies the occurrence of famous miracles, suggests they could be due to natural properties or magic, and argues that even if they occur, they do not necessarily indicate truth. Understanding this objection is essential for appreciating the response of Ahl al-Haqq that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the skeptical denial
Carefully read the opening where the skeptic denies the reported miracles of the prophets. Notice the specific examples given (staff, resurrection, etc.) and the claim that such events are impossible.
The skeptic is not just doubting but asserting impossibility.
2
Identify the alternative explanations
Identify the alternative explanations the skeptic offers: that extraordinary events can be due to the properties of things, magic, or occult sciences. Note the list of such sciences (incantation, astrology, etc.).
3
Analyze the argument about indication
Focus on the logical argument that a miracle only indicates the agent's power, not truthfulness. Understand the point about conjunction: that an event coinciding with a claim does not prove the claim, just as any other coincidence wouldn't.
4
Reflect on the inconsistency about false claimants
Note the final point: if miracles can occur at the hands of false claimants to divinity, why would they prove prophethood? This sets up the need for a criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الكلام على بينة الدعوى فنحن أولا ننكر ما حكيتموه عن الأنبياء من قلب العصا حية، وإحياء الموتى، وفلق البحر، وخروج الناقة من الصخرة الصماء، وتسبيح الحصى، وانشقاق القمر، فإن جنس ذلك مستحيل الوجود فنحن أولا نمنع حصولها، فماذا دليلكم على وقوع ذلك؟ ثم بم تنكرون على من يرد الخوارق إلى خواص الأشياء؟ فإنا نجد حصول أمثال ذلك من الجمادات على يد من لا دين له كالأمطار التي تحصل من اصطكاك الأحجار وكالرياح التي تهب تحريك ما مخصوص ثم التعزيم والتنجيم والتبخير، وعلم الطلسمات، واستسخار الروحانيات واستخدام الكواكب العلوية علوم معروفة والعمل بها من العجائب المعجزة والغرائب المفحمة، فما أنكرتم أن ما أتى به هذا المدعي من جنس ذلك ثم الواجب عليكم أن تثبتوا وجه دلالة المعجزة على الصدق، فإنه من حيث هو فعل دل على قدرة الفاعل فقط من هذا الوجه لم يدل على صدق قول المدعي من حيث اقترانه بدعواه لم يدل أيضاً؛ لأن اقترانه بدعواه كاقترانه بحدوث حادث آخر من قول أو عمل، ثم لم يدل نفس الاقتران على حق أو باطل، فكيف دل هاهنا؟ وأيضا فإن عندكم يجوز خرق العادات على يدي مدعي الإلهية، ولم يدل ذلك على صدق دعواه، فكيف يدل على صدق دعوى النبوة؟ قال أهل الحق : قام الدليل على أن الرب تعالى خالق الخلق ومالكهم، له أن يتصرف في عباده بالأمر والنهي، وله أن يختار له الأمر والخلق والملك ومن واحدًا لتعريف أمره ونهيه فيبلغ عنه إليهم، فإن من له الخلق والإبداع له ...
As for discourse concerning the evidence of the claim, we first deny what you have narrated from the prophets: the turning of a staff into a snake, bringing the dead to life, splitting the sea, the emergence of a she-camel from a solid rock, the glorification of pebbles, and the splitting of the moon. For the kind of these things is impossible of existence, so we first deny their occurrence. So what is your proof of their occurrence? Then how do you reject someone who attributes extraordinary occurrences to the properties of things? For we find the occurrence of similar things from inanimate objects at the hands of one who has no religion, like rain that comes from the collision of stones, and winds that blow from a specific type of movement, then incantations, astrology, fumigation, the science of talismans, evocation of spirits, and use of celestial bodies—these are well-known sciences, and working with them produces amazing wonders and astounding marvels. So why do you not accept that what this claimant has brought is of that kind? Then you are obligated to prove the aspect of the miracle's indication of truthfulness. For insofar as it is an act, it indicates only the power of the agent; from this aspect it does not indicate the truthfulness of the claimant's statement, and from the aspect of its conjunction with his claim it also does not indicate, because its conjunction with his claim is like its conjunction with the occurrence of another event, whether a statement or an act. Then the conjunction itself does not indicate truth or falsehood—so how does it indicate here? Also, according to you, it is permissible for violation of norms to occur at the hands of one claiming divinity, and that does not indicate the truth of his claim, so how does it indicate the truth of the claim of prophethood? The People of Truth said: The proof has been established that the Lord, exalted, is the Creator of creation and their Owner; He has the right to dispose of His servants by command and prohibition, and He may choose for Himself—from command, creation, and dominion—one person to define His command and prohibition, so that he may convey from Him to them. For He who possesses creation and origination has...
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage presents a skeptical objection against miracles as proof of prophethood and then begins the response of Ahl al-Haqq. The objection first denies the occurrence of famous miracles (staff, resurrection, etc.) as inherently impossible, demanding proof of their occurrence. Then it argues that even if such extraordinary events occur, they could be due to natural properties or magical arts, which are known to produce wonders. Therefore, a miracle (mu'jiza) does not automatically prove truthfulness; it only indicates the agent's power. Its conjunction with a claim does not make it indicative of truth, just as any event coinciding with a statement does not prove that statement. Additionally, if miracles can occur at the hands of false claimants to divinity, why not for prophethood? Then the response of Ahl al-Haqq begins: God is the Creator and Owner, with full authority to command and prohibit. He may choose a messenger to convey His commands. This establishes the basis for distinguishing true miracles from magic.

Key Terms
بينة الدعوى
خوارق
معجزة
خواص الأشياء
تعزيم
تنجيم
طلسمات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any extraordinary event accompanying a claim of prophethood automatically proves the claimant's truthfulness.
Correction: The objection argues that such events could be due to natural or magical causes, and even if miraculous, they only show power, not truthfulness. Additional reasoning is needed.

Checkpoint
According to the skeptical objection, why does the conjunction of a miracle with a claim not prove the claim's truth?
A) Because miracles are impossible.
B) Because the conjunction is coincidental, like any other event happening at the same time.
C) Because prophets are known to be liars.
D) Because only God can perform miracles.

Key Takeaway
The skeptic challenges the evidentiary value of miracles, arguing they could be natural or magical and do not inherently prove truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever internally questioned whether a reported miracle might have a natural or magical explanation? What is your honest reaction to the skeptic’s challenge that miracles could be mere coincidence?
?
If you were asked by a non-believer to prove that the Prophet’s miracles are truly divine and not just tricks, could you give a convincing answer? Trace your own reasoning: do you rely on the event itself or on something else?
?
The skeptic argues that a miracle only shows power, not truthfulness. This forces you to examine the foundation of your faith: Is your belief in prophethood based on the fact that these events happened, or on the character and message of the Prophet? Are you willing to face that question without flinching?

Miracles
intermediate
5 min
The Response of Ahl al-Haqq
Response of Ahl al-Haqq based on God's sovereignty and messenger selection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational argument of Ahl al-Haqq that God's absolute sovereignty and authority to command necessitate the sending of messengers, and that true miracles are distinguished from magic by being beyond natural and magical means.

Core Idea
God's ownership and authority justify the selection of messengers who perform miracles as proof.

After presenting the skeptical objection, the text now gives the response of Ahl al-Haqq (the People of Truth). This response establishes the theological basis for prophethood: God is the Creator and Owner of all, and He has the right to command His servants. From this right, it follows that He may choose a messenger to convey His commands. This provides the framework in which miracles serve as divine confirmation.

Guided Path
1
Read the response carefully
Read the passage from 'The People of Truth said' onwards. Notice how it starts with a statement of God's attributes as Creator and Owner.
This is a fundamental premise for the argument.
2
Understand God's right to command
Recognize that because God is the Creator and Owner, He has the authority to issue commands and prohibitions to His servants.
3
Understand the selection of a messenger
See that from this authority, God may choose a specific person to define and convey His commands. This messenger is distinguished by divine support, which is the miracle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما الكلام على بينة الدعوى فنحن أولا ننكر ما حكيتموه عن الأنبياء من قلب العصا حية، وإحياء الموتى، وفلق البحر، وخروج الناقة من الصخرة الصماء، وتسبيح الحصى، وانشقاق القمر، فإن جنس ذلك مستحيل الوجود فنحن أولا نمنع حصولها، فماذا دليلكم على وقوع ذلك؟ ثم بم تنكرون على من يرد الخوارق إلى خواص الأشياء؟ فإنا نجد حصول أمثال ذلك من الجمادات على يد من لا دين له كالأمطار التي تحصل من اصطكاك الأحجار وكالرياح التي تهب تحريك ما مخصوص ثم التعزيم والتنجيم والتبخير، وعلم الطلسمات، واستسخار الروحانيات واستخدام الكواكب العلوية علوم معروفة والعمل بها من العجائب المعجزة والغرائب المفحمة، فما أنكرتم أن ما أتى به هذا المدعي من جنس ذلك ثم الواجب عليكم أن تثبتوا وجه دلالة المعجزة على الصدق، فإنه من حيث هو فعل دل على قدرة الفاعل فقط من هذا الوجه لم يدل على صدق قول المدعي من حيث اقترانه بدعواه لم يدل أيضاً؛ لأن اقترانه بدعواه كاقترانه بحدوث حادث آخر من قول أو عمل، ثم لم يدل نفس الاقتران على حق أو باطل، فكيف دل هاهنا؟ وأيضا فإن عندكم يجوز خرق العادات على يدي مدعي الإلهية، ولم يدل ذلك على صدق دعواه، فكيف يدل على صدق دعوى النبوة؟ قال أهل الحق : قام الدليل على أن الرب تعالى خالق الخلق ومالكهم، له أن يتصرف في عباده بالأمر والنهي، وله أن يختار له الأمر والخلق والملك ومن واحدًا لتعريف أمره ونهيه فيبلغ عنه إليهم، فإن من له الخلق والإبداع له ...

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq, what right does God have because He is the Creator and Owner?
A) The right to grant miracles to anyone.
B) The right to dispose of His servants by command and prohibition.
C) The right to change the laws of nature.
D) The right to forgive all sins.

Key Takeaway
God's absolute sovereignty provides the basis for sending messengers, which then allows miracles to function as divine confirmation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly submit to every command and prohibition from the Messenger (peace be upon him) as an expression of God's absolute sovereignty over you, or do you rationalize exceptions based on your desires? Where today are you resisting His authority?
?
If God chose a specific messenger for your guidance, what does your level of engagement with his message say about your acceptance of God's right to choose? How much time do you spend learning his commands compared to pursuing your own plans?
?
When you hear the command of God, do you hesitate because you think you know better, or do you immediately obey? Which area of your life requires you to repent from putting your own judgment above that of the chosen messenger?

Miracles
beginner
6 min
Objection Against Miracles as Evidence
The mutakallimun present an objection to miracle-based proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational objections raised against using miracles as direct proof for a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles alone do not automatically prove truthfulness.

Theologians (mutakallimun) often rely on miracles to confirm prophethood, but this argument is not immune to challenge. In this passage, an objector raises several points: amazing acts can be produced by non-believers, a miracle only indicates power not truthfulness, and its conjunction with a claim is meaningless. This lesson examines these objections.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage of the objection carefully, then read the literal translation. Notice the multiple arguments presented.
The objector uses examples like rain from stones and magic.
2
Identify the three main arguments
Find the points: (1) similar acts from non-believers, (2) miracle only indicates power, not truth, (3) conjunction with claim doesn't indicate truth, (4) analogy with false claimants of divinity.
These are listed in the commentary.
3
Understand the logical structure
Notice how each argument challenges a different aspect of the miracle-proof connection.
4
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: If these objections stand, how could a miracle ever serve as evidence? This sets up the need for a response.
The response comes in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من خواص الأشياء؟ فإنا نجد حصول أمثال ذلك من الجمادات على يد من لا دين له كالأمطار التي تحصل من اصطكاك الأحجار وكالرياح التي تهب تحريك ما مخصوص ثم التعزيم والتنجيم والتبخير، وعلم الطلسمات، واستسخار الروحانيات واستخدام الكواكب العلوية علوم معروفة والعمل بها من العجائب المعجزة والغرائب المفحمة، فما أنكرتم أن ما أتى به هذا المدعي من جنس ذلك ثم الواجب عليكم أن تثبتوا وجه دلالة المعجزة على الصدق، فإنه من حيث هو فعل دل على قدرة الفاعل فقط من هذا الوجه لم يدل على صدق قول المدعي من حيث اقترانه بدعواه لم يدل أيضاً؛ لأن اقترانه بدعواه كاقترانه بحدوث حادث آخر من قول أو عمل، ثم لم يدل نفس الاقتران على حق أو باطل، فكيف دل هاهنا؟ وأيضا فإن عندكم يجوز خرق العادات على يدي مدعي الإلهية، ولم يدل ذلك على صدق دعواه، فكيف يدل على صدق دعوى النبوة؟ قال أهل الحق: قام الدليل على أن الرب تعالى خالق الخلق ومالكهم، له أن يتصرف في عباده بالأمر والنهي، وله أن يختار له الأمر والخلق والملك ومن واحدًا لتعريف أمره ونهيه فيبلغ عنه إليهم، فإن من له الخلق والإبداع له الاختيار والاصطفاء وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَخْتَارُ، فلا استحالة في هذه المراتب، ولا استحالة في نفس الدعوى، ولا يضاهي استحالته استحالة دعوى الإلهية، بل هو من الجائزات العقلية فله الواجبات الحكمية، فبقي كون الخبر والدعوى على احتمال الصدق والكذب، وإنما ترجح الصدق على الكذب بدليل.
From the properties of things? For we find the occurrence of such things from inanimate objects by the hand of one who has no religion, like rain that occurs from the striking of stones, and winds that blow by moving something specific, then incantations, astrology, fumigation, the science of talismans, compelling spirits, and using the higher stars—known sciences, and working with them results in amazing miracles and astounding marvels. So why do you deny that what this claimant has brought is of that kind? Then it is incumbent upon you to establish the aspect of the miracle's indication of truthfulness. For insofar as it is an act, it indicates only the power of the agent; from this aspect it does not indicate the truthfulness of the claimant's statement. Insofar as it is conjoined with his claim, it also does not indicate; because its conjunction with his claim is like its conjunction with the occurrence of another event, whether a statement or action, and the conjunction itself does not indicate truth or falsehood, so how does it indicate here? And also, according to you, the breaking of habits is permissible at the hand of one who claims divinity, and that does not indicate the truth of his claim, so how does it indicate the truth of the claim of prophethood? The people of truth said: The proof is established that the Lord, exalted, is the Creator of creation and their Owner. He may dispose of His servants by command and prohibition, and He may choose for Himself the command, creation, and dominion, and [choose] one person to define His command and prohibition, so that he may convey from Him to them. For He who has creation and origination has choice and selection. 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses.' So there is no impossibility in these ranks, nor is there impossibility in the claim itself, nor does its impossibility resemble the impossibility of the claim of divinity. Rather, it is among the rational possibilities, so it has normative obligations. Thus the report and the claim remain subject to probability of truth and falsehood, and the truth is only preponderated over falsehood by a proof.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the standard use of miracles to confirm prophethood, then responds. The objector argues that many amazing acts are produced by non-believers through natural or magical means, so the miracle might be of that kind. Moreover, a miracle as an act only indicates power, not truthfulness; its conjunction with a claim doesn't add indication. Even if you allow miracles for false gods, how then for prophets? The response from Ahl al-Haqq establishes that the claim of prophethood is possible because God is the sole Creator and Owner, and He can choose a messenger; it's not like the impossible claim of divinity. The claim remains uncertain until a proof preponderates truth over falsehood. This sets up the need for the theologians' methods.

Key Terms
معجزة
صدق
دعوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A miracle directly and automatically proves the truth of a claimant's prophethood.
Correction: This passage shows that a miracle as an act only indicates power; its conjunction with a claim does not automatically indicate truth. Further proof is needed to preponderate truth over falsehood.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, why does the conjunction of a miracle with a claim not indicate truth?
A) Because the miracle is too weak.
B) Because conjunction is like any other coincidental event.
C) Because the claimant is lying.
D) Because miracles only happen to true prophets.

Key Takeaway
Miracles alone are insufficient to prove truthfulness; they require additional reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness something extraordinary that seems to confirm a religious claim, how do you ensure you are not being swayed by spectacle rather than seeking genuine truth? What step from this lesson can you apply the next time you hear a claim supported by an apparent miracle?
?
The passage argues that a miracle, on its own, only shows power, not truth. Has there been a time in your life when you were impressed by someone's abilities but later realized their character or message was false? How does this shape your responsibility to examine claims more carefully?
?
This objection forces you to consider that even the most astonishing sign requires intellectual scrutiny. Are you willing to question miraculous claims even when they come from those you trust? Commit to one practical way you will apply this principle in your faith journey.

Response of Ahl al-Haqq: Possibility of Prophethood
Ahl al-Haqq provide a rational defense of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational foundation for prophethood and why the objection does not undermine its possibility.

Core Idea
Prophethood is rationally possible because God is the Creator and can choose messengers.

After the objection, the people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq) respond by establishing the rational possibility of prophethood. They argue that since God is the sole Creator and Owner of creation, He has the right to command and choose messengers. Unlike the impossible claim of divinity, prophethood is among rational possibilities. However, the truth of a specific claimant still requires proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the response passage
Read the Arabic response passage and its translation. Notice the logical flow from God's attributes to the possibility of prophethood.
The passage includes a Quranic verse (28:68).
2
Identify the key premises
Find the premises: God is Creator and Owner; He can command and choose; prophethood is possible; claim of prophethood is not impossible like divinity.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that the claim of prophethood remains subject to truth and falsehood, and only a proof can tilt it toward truth.
This implies that miracles alone aren't enough; a proof (daeel) is needed.
4
Connect to the objection
Notice how this response counters the objection by showing that prophethood is rationally possible, unlike divinity, and that the claim needs proof, not automatic acceptance.

من خواص الأشياء؟ فإنا نجد حصول أمثال ذلك من الجمادات على يد من لا دين له كالأمطار التي تحصل من اصطكاك الأحجار وكالرياح التي تهب تحريك ما مخصوص ثم التعزيم والتنجيم والتبخير، وعلم الطلسمات، واستسخار الروحانيات واستخدام الكواكب العلوية علوم معروفة والعمل بها من العجائب المعجزة والغرائب المفحمة، فما أنكرتم أن ما أتى به هذا المدعي من جنس ذلك ثم الواجب عليكم أن تثبتوا وجه دلالة المعجزة على الصدق، فإنه من حيث هو فعل دل على قدرة الفاعل فقط من هذا الوجه لم يدل على صدق قول المدعي من حيث اقترانه بدعواه لم يدل أيضاً؛ لأن اقترانه بدعواه كاقترانه بحدوث حادث آخر من قول أو عمل، ثم لم يدل نفس الاقتران على حق أو باطل، فكيف دل هاهنا؟ وأيضا فإن عندكم يجوز خرق العادات على يدي مدعي الإلهية، ولم يدل ذلك على صدق دعواه، فكيف يدل على صدق دعوى النبوة؟ قال أهل الحق: قام الدليل على أن الرب تعالى خالق الخلق ومالكهم، له أن يتصرف في عباده بالأمر والنهي، وله أن يختار له الأمر والخلق والملك ومن واحدًا لتعريف أمره ونهيه فيبلغ عنه إليهم، فإن من له الخلق والإبداع له الاختيار والاصطفاء وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَخْتَارُ، فلا استحالة في هذه المراتب، ولا استحالة في نفس الدعوى، ولا يضاهي استحالته استحالة دعوى الإلهية، بل هو من الجائزات العقلية فله الواجبات الحكمية، فبقي كون الخبر والدعوى على احتمال الصدق والكذب، وإنما ترجح الصدق على الكذب بدليل.
From the properties of things? For we find the occurrence of such things from inanimate objects by the hand of one who has no religion, like rain that occurs from the striking of stones, and winds that blow by moving something specific, then incantations, astrology, fumigation, the science of talismans, compelling spirits, and using the higher stars—known sciences, and working with them results in amazing miracles and astounding marvels. So why do you deny that what this claimant has brought is of that kind? Then it is incumbent upon you to establish the aspect of the miracle's indication of truthfulness. For insofar as it is an act, it indicates only the power of the agent; from this aspect it does not indicate the truthfulness of the claimant's statement. Insofar as it is conjoined with his claim, it also does not indicate; because its conjunction with his claim is like its conjunction with the occurrence of another event, whether a statement or action, and the conjunction itself does not indicate truth or falsehood, so how does it indicate here? And also, according to you, the breaking of habits is permissible at the hand of one who claims divinity, and that does not indicate the truth of his claim, so how does it indicate the truth of the claim of prophethood? The people of truth said: The proof is established that the Lord, exalted, is the Creator of creation and their Owner. He may dispose of His servants by command and prohibition, and He may choose for Himself the command, creation, and dominion, and [choose] one person to define His command and prohibition, so that he may convey from Him to them. For He who has creation and origination has choice and selection. 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses.' So there is no impossibility in these ranks, nor is there impossibility in the claim itself, nor does its impossibility resemble the impossibility of the claim of divinity. Rather, it is among the rational possibilities, so it has normative obligations. Thus the report and the claim remain subject to probability of truth and falsehood, and the truth is only preponderated over falsehood by a proof.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the standard use of miracles to confirm prophethood, then responds. The objector argues that many amazing acts are produced by non-believers through natural or magical means, so the miracle might be of that kind. Moreover, a miracle as an act only indicates power, not truthfulness; its conjunction with a claim doesn't add indication. Even if you allow miracles for false gods, how then for prophets? The response from Ahl al-Haqq establishes that the claim of prophethood is possible because God is the sole Creator and Owner, and He can choose a messenger; it's not like the impossible claim of divinity. The claim remains uncertain until a proof preponderates truth over falsehood. This sets up the need for the theologians' methods.

Key Terms
جوائز عقلية
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood claims are automatically false because they involve extraordinary events.
Correction: The passage argues that prophethood is rationally possible because God is the Owner of creation and can send messengers. It is not impossible like divinity claims.

Checkpoint
According to the response, why is the claim of prophethood not impossible like the claim of divinity?
A) Because prophets are more powerful.
B) Because prophethood is among rational possibilities.
C) Because miracles prove it.
D) Because the claimant is sincere.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is rationally possible; its truth requires a proof beyond the mere occurrence of miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in prophethood. But is your belief based on a rational conviction that it is possible, or is it simply inherited? This lesson says prophethood is possible but needs proof. Have you ever sought that proof for yourself, or are you relying on others?
?
If you met someone who denied the possibility of prophethood, how would you respond using the reasoning from this passage? Would your answer be rooted in clear premises, or would it be emotional? Examine your heart: are you ready to defend this rationally, or are you merely repeating what you've heard?
?
The passage distinguishes the claim of prophethood from the claim of divinity. Have you ever conflated the two in your mind, thinking any claim to divine communication is automatically false? This lesson demands you face the possibility that God can speak to humans through messengers. How does that change your urgency to listen to the Prophet's message today?

The Miracle as Divine Affirmation: The First Method
The mutakallimun present the first method: the conjunction of a miracle with a claim is equivalent to verbal affirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the conjunction of a miracle with a prophetic claim and challenge is considered equivalent to God's verbal affirmation, and how the analogy of the king behind the curtain illustrates this rational proof.

Core Idea
A miracle is God's silent 'yes' to a prophet's claim when the context is right.

The theologians developed rational arguments to prove that miracles indicate prophethood. Their first method draws an analogy between a miracle and a king moving a curtain in response to a messenger's request. In this lesson, you will see how the combination of miracle, challenge, and claim creates a decisive proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before interpreting.
Notice how the passage first states the principle, then explains the conditions, then gives the analogy.
2
Identify the key conditions
The passage lists conditions that make the miracle a decisive proof: knowledge of God's sunna, the occurrence of a miracle at the time of challenge and summons, and the combination of these conditions. Identify each.
The phrase 'اجتماع هذه الأركان' indicates that all conditions must come together.
3
Understand the analogy of the king and the curtain
The passage uses a vivid analogy: a king behind a curtain, a crowd, a messenger who asks for a sign, and the curtain moving. Reflect on how this mirrors the prophetic claim and the miracle.
The king's action of moving the curtain 'على خلاف العادة' is analogous to God's miraculous intervention.
4
Connect the analogy to the divine context
Just as the king's curtain movement affirms the messenger, God's miracle affirms the prophet. Ask yourself why this analogy is logically compelling.
The analogy highlights that the miracle is not arbitrary but occurs in response to a claim and challenge.
5
Conclude why this is a valid proof
Understand that this method establishes that the miracle itself, when conditions are met, is equivalent to God's verbal affirmation. This is the foundation for the other methods.
This method is called 'التصديق بالفعل' (affirmation by action).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمتكلمين طرق في إثبات المرجح ; أحدها أن اقتران المعجزة بدعوى النبي نازل منزلة التصديق بالقول، وذلك أنه متى عرف من سنة الله تعالى أنه لا يظهر أمرًا خارقا للعادة على يدي من يدعي الرسالة عند وقت التحدي والاستدعاء إلا لتصديقه فيما يجري به، واجتماع هذه الأركان انتهض قرينة قطعية دالة على صدق المدعي، فكان المعجزة بالفعل كالتصديق شفاه بالقول، ونحن نعلم قطعا في صورة من يدعي الرسالة من ملك حاضر محتجب بستر، والجماعة على كثرتها حضور ثم إن رجلا من عرض الناس إذا قام بين يدي ذلك الجمع الكثير من الخلق، وقال: أيها الناس إني رسول هذا الملك إليكم، وآية صدقي في دعواي أنه يحرك هذا الستر إذا استدعيت منه، ثم قال: أيها الملك إن كنت صادقا في دعواي الرسالة عنك فحرك هذا الستر، فحرك في الحال، علم قطعا ويقينا بقرينة الحال أنه أراد بذلك الفعل تصديق المدعي، ونزل التحريك منه على خلاف العادة منزلة التصديق
The theologians have methods for establishing the preponderating factor; one of them is that the conjunction of the miracle with the prophet's claim takes the place of verbal affirmation. That is, when it is known from the sunna of God that He does not produce a miraculous event at the hand of one who claims prophethood at the time of challenge and summons except to affirm him in what he proclaims, and the combination of these conditions constitutes a decisive indication of the truthfulness of the claimant. Thus the miracle in action is like an oral affirmation by speech. And we know with certainty in the situation of one who claims prophethood from a present king veiled by a curtain, with a large crowd present. Then if a man from the common people stands before that great assembly of people and says, 'O people, I am the messenger of this king to you, and the sign of my truthfulness in my claim is that he will move this curtain when I request it from him,' then he says, 'O king, if I am truthful in my claim of being a messenger from you, then move this curtain,' and he moves it immediately, we know with certainty and conviction by the circumstance of the situation that he intended by that act to affirm the claimant, and the movement from him, contrary to custom, takes the place of affirmation.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage presents the first method of the theologians to prove that a miracle indicates truth. It argues that the miracle, when accompanied by a claim of prophethood and a challenge, is equivalent to God saying 'He is truthful.' The analogy of the king behind a curtain illustrates: if a person claims to be the king's messenger and asks the king to move the curtain as a sign, and the curtain moves, everyone understands that as confirmation. Similarly, God's habit is that He only performs a miracle at the hand of a true prophet under challenge. So the miracle itself, in that context, is a decisive proof.

Key Terms
معجزة
اقتران
تصديق
سنة الله
قرينة قطعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A miracle is proof by itself, regardless of context.
Correction: This method emphasizes that the miracle must occur in the context of a challenge and a claim. Without these conditions, the miracle does not serve as a decisive proof.

Checkpoint
According to the first method, when does a miracle become a decisive proof of prophethood?
A) When it is extremely powerful.
B) When it occurs in the context of a challenge with a claim.
C) When it happens many times.
D) When it is seen by many.

Key Takeaway
A miracle, when it occurs in response to a prophetic challenge and claim, is equivalent to God's direct verbal affirmation of the prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the certainty of the crowd in the analogy — that they knew without doubt the king intended affirmation — do you feel that same level of certainty about the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him)? If not, what is holding you back, and will you actively seek to remove that barrier today?
?
The passage says the miracle is like God speaking 'yes' directly to the prophet's claim. How does this change the way you view the miracles mentioned in the Qur'an? Will you now take them as personal affirmations from God to you, strengthening your faith?
?
If you were in that assembly and saw the curtain move, would you have immediately believed? What does your answer reveal about your readiness to accept truth when God provides clear signs? How will you cultivate that readiness in your daily life?

The Three Elements of Prophetic Evidence
The author explains how miracles combined with claims and lack of opposition produce certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the combination of a miracle, a claim, and lack of opposition forms cumulative evidence (qara'in) that certifies a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles alone are not proof; they need a claim and no opposition.

The author of Nihayat al-Aqdam argues that certainty about a prophet's truthfulness does not come from a single proof but from the convergence of multiple contextual evidences. In this passage, he identifies three essential components that together function like a verbal attestation. Let's examine how they work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins mid-sentence, but it is a complete argument.
2
Identify the three elements of Qara'in
The passage lists three components that together form the cumulative evidence. Find each one and understand its role.
The three are: the miracle, the claim, and lack of opposition.
3
Understand the function of Qara'in
The author says these qara'in 'take the place of verbal attestation' (nazala manzilat al-tasdiq bi'l-qawl). Think about what that means logically.
Qara'in are not the same as direct testimony but serve the same epistemic function.
4
Reflect on the necessity of all three
Why must the miracle be accompanied by a claim and be free from opposition? Consider how each element contributes to eliminating doubt.
This connects to the common misunderstanding that a miracle alone suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالقول، ولم يشك واحد من أهل الجمع أن الأمر على ما يجري به المدعي، فكذلك في صورة مسألتنا هذه، فإذا المرجح للصدق هي القرائن الحاصلة من اجتماع أمور كثيرة ؛ منها الخارق للعادة ومنها كونه مقرونا بالدعوى، ومنها سلامته عن المعارضة، فانتهضت هذه القرائن بمجموعها دالة على صدق المدعي نازلة منزلة التصديق بالقول، وذلك مثل العلم الحاصل من سائر القرائن ؛ أعني قرائن الحال وقرائن المقال.
By the statement, and none of the people of consensus doubted that the matter proceeds as the claimant states, so likewise in the case of our question here: the determinant for truthfulness are the contextual evidences (qara'in) resulting from the combination of many things: among them the miracle breaking the norm, and among them its being accompanied by the claim, and among them its being free from opposition. So these contextual evidences as a whole indicate the truthfulness of the claimant, taking the place of verbal attestation. That is like the knowledge obtained from other contextual evidences—I mean contextual evidences of state and contextual evidences of speech.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of contextual evidence (qara'in) that collectively indicate the truthfulness of a claimant to prophecy. The author states that no one from the people of consensus doubts that the matter proceeds as the claimant says. So in our case, the determinant of truthfulness are the qara'in arising from the combination of many things: the miracle (khariq lil'ada), its being accompanied by the claim (da'wa), and its being free from opposition (mu'arada). These qara'in together indicate the truthfulness of the claimant, taking the place of verbal attestation. This is like knowledge obtained from other qara'in, namely those of state (hal) and speech (maqal).

Key Terms
القرائن (qara'in)
الخارق للعادة (khariq lil'ada)
الدعوى (da'wa)
المعارضة (mu'arada)
قرائن الحال (qara'in al-hal)
قرائن المقال (qara'in al-maqal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A miracle alone is sufficient proof of prophecy.
Correction: The author argues that a miracle must be accompanied by a claim of prophecy and be free from opposition to constitute proof.

Checkpoint
What three elements combine to form the qara'in that indicate a prophet's truthfulness?
A) The miracle, the prophet's knowledge, and his lineage
B) The miracle, the claim, and lack of opposition
C) The miracle, the number of followers, and time
D) The prophecy itself, the message, and the signs

Key Takeaway
Certainty in prophecy is achieved through the convergence of a miracle, a claim, and the absence of opposition, forming cumulative contextual evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says that qara'in as a whole produce certainty like verbal testimony. When you think about your own conviction in Islam, have you ever consciously examined the three qara'in (miracle, claim, no opposition) for the Prophet Muhammad? If not, what will you do this week to study one of them in detail?
?
If you saw a miracle today, would you immediately believe the person is a prophet? According to this lesson, you need all three elements. Are you prone to being swayed by emotional experiences without checking the claim and absence of opposition? Commit to not trusting any spiritual experience without evaluating it against the three criteria.
?
The author mentions 'consensus' that no one doubted when multiple indicators align. Yet many people today doubt prophethood. What qara'in are they missing? Specifically, what is one qara'in that you personally need to strengthen your certainty? Write it down and a specific time to investigate it.

The Miracle as Response to Prayer: A Proof of Prophecy
The author argues that a miracle in response to prayer proves the prophet's truthfulness and cannot come from a liar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a miracle that occurs as a response to a claimant's prayer demonstrates his truthfulness and the validity of his prophecy, and why it cannot come from a liar.

Core Idea
A miracle in direct response to a claim proves the claimant cannot be lying.

This lesson presents a second argument for the truthfulness of a prophet: the miracle as a prayer answered by God. The author explains how this sign, when linked to the prophetic claim, establishes a state of truthfulness with God. He also addresses potential objections about saints and magicians, showing that the proof remains sound.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Observe the author's logical flow and the key terms.
Notice the conditional reasoning: 'if the supplicant were supposed to be a liar... then the evidence of truth would turn into evidence of falsehood.'
2
Identify the key components
Identify the 'miracle', 'prayer of the supplicant', 'claim', 'truthfulness', and 'contradiction'. Understand how they relate.
The miracle is not just any miracle; it is specifically a response to the prayer of the one claiming prophecy.
3
Understand the conditional argument
The author argues that if the claimant were a liar, the miracle would become evidence of falsehood, which is contradictory. Think about why this contradiction is impossible.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: assuming the opposite leads to a logical contradiction.
4
Address the objections
The author raises cases of saints and magicians. He explains the condition: the miracle must be in direct response to the claim at the time of the claim. Later changes do not affect the proof.
A saint's future fall or a magician's trick does not involve a prophetic claim in the same way.
5
Reflect on the analogy and conclusion
The author draws an analogy: just as a sign of power cannot indicate weakness, a sign of truth cannot indicate falsehood. He concludes that this method is superior.
Why might this method be better than the first? Consider that it ties the miracle directly to the claimant's claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه آخر الآية الخارقة للعادة كما دلت بوقوعها على قدرة الفاعل وباختصاصها على إرادته وبأحكامها على علمه كذلك دلت بوقوعها مستجابة لدعاء الداعي لا لدعوى المدعي على أن له عند الله حالة صدق ومقالة حق، ومن كانت دعوته مستجابة عند الله يستحيل أن يكون في دعواه كاذبًا على الله تعالى وهذا هو حقيقة النبوة، وذلك أن استجابته في أمور لا يقدر الخلق على ذلك دليل على صدق هذا الداعي، ولو قدر الداعي كاذبًا في نفسه على الله أقبح كذب وهو الرسالة عنه بما لم يرسل انقلبت دليل الصدق دليلا على الكذب وهو متناقض.
ونحن لا ننكر أن يكون شخص من الأشخاص مستجاب الدعوة ثم ينقلب حاله إلى حالة الأشقياء، كما لا ننكر أن يظهر خارق للعادة على يد ساحر، لكن الشرط في الأمرين واحد ؛ وهو أن يكون المدعي في حال ما يدعي مستجاب الدعوة بالآية حتى تكون الآية دالة على صدق حالته ودرجته عند الله تعالى، وإذا قدر كونه كاذبا انقلبت الدلالة على الصدق دلالة على الكذب، وهو محال لتناقضه، وكما أن الوقوع إذا دل على القدرة لم يدل على العجز والإحكام لما دل على العلم لم يدل على الجهل ، كذلك دليل الصدق لا يجوز أن يكون دليلا على الكذب، وهذه الطريقة أحسن من الأولى.
Another aspect: the miraculous sign breaking the norm, just as it indicates by its occurrence the power of the agent, by its specificity His will, and by its perfection His knowledge, likewise it indicates by its occurrence as a response to the prayer of the supplicant, not to the claim of the claimant, that he has with God a state of truthfulness and a right speech. Whoever's prayer is answered by God is impossible to be in his claim a liar against God Almighty, and this is the reality of prophecy. That is because His answering him in matters that the creation cannot accomplish is evidence of the truthfulness of this supplicant. If the supplicant were supposed to be a liar in himself against God with the ugliest lie—which is the message from Him that He did not send—then the evidence of truth would turn into evidence of falsehood, which is contradictory. We do not deny that a person may be answered in his prayer and then his state turns to a state of the wretched, just as we do not deny that a miracle may appear at the hand of a sorcerer. However, the condition in both matters is one: that the claimant, at the time of his claim, be answered in prayer by the miracle, so that the miracle indicates the truthfulness of his state and his rank with God. If he is supposed to be a liar, then the indication of truth becomes an indication of falsehood, which is impossible due to its contradiction. And just as occurrence when it indicates power does not indicate incapacity, and perfection when it indicates knowledge does not indicate ignorance, likewise the evidence of truth cannot be evidence of falsehood. And this method is better than the first.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a second proof for the truthfulness of a prophet through miracles. The author argues that the miraculous sign (aya khariqa lil'ada) indicates God's power, will, and knowledge. Similarly, when it occurs as a response to the supplicant's prayer (not to the claim itself), it indicates that the supplicant has a state of truthfulness with God. Such a person cannot be lying about God. The author then addresses objections: miracles can occur from saints or magicians, but the condition is that the miracle must be in direct response to the claim of prophecy at that moment. If the claimant were a liar, the miracle would become evidence of falsehood, which is contradictory. This is like how a sign of power cannot indicate weakness. The author concludes that this method is better than the earlier one.

Key Terms
الآية الخارقة للعادة (al-aya al-khariqa lil'ada)
دعاء الداعي (du'a' al-da'i)
حالة صدق (halat sidq)
حقيقة النبوة (haqiqat al-nubuwwa)
التناقض (tanaqud)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that miracles performed by saints or magicians disprove the proof that miracles from God prove a prophet's truthfulness.
Correction: The author clarifies that the miracle must be in direct response to the prophetic claim at the moment of the claim. A saint's later fall or a magician's trick does not occur as a direct response to a claim of prophecy.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why can't a miracle that responds to a claimant's prayer come from a liar?
A) Because miracles only happen to truthful people;
B) Because if he were lying, the miracle would indicate falsehood, which is contradictory;
C) Because magicians cannot produce true miracles;
D) Because the claim must be about God's message.

Key Takeaway
A miracle that is a direct response to a prophetic claim logically proves the claimant's truthfulness, as a liar would create an impossible contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray for something that only God can grant, do you examine your own heart to see if you are in a 'state of truthfulness' (halat sidq) with Him? What would it mean for you to receive an answered prayer while you are knowingly hiding a lie in your life?
?
The author says that if a claimant were a liar, the miracle would become evidence of falsehood—a contradiction God would never allow. Have you ever been tempted to claim a spiritual experience to prove your own righteousness? How does this argument expose the danger of self-deception?
?
Imagine you are waiting for a sign from God to confirm a difficult decision. This lesson says that a true sign is a direct response to a sincere prayer, not just any coincidence. Are you willing to put your request to that test, or would you rather cling to ambiguous signs that let you avoid accountability?

Classification of Miracles and the Role of Challenge
The author classifies miracles into preventive and affirmative types and discusses the role of challenge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two-fold classification of miracles into preventive and affirmative types and how the concept of challenge (tahaddi) serves as evidence of prophetic truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles are either prevention of the customary or affirmation of the non-customary; both are tied to the prophet's challenge.

In this passage, the author presents a third argument linking the contextual evidence of truthfulness (qarinat al-sidq) to the prophet's challenge. He then classifies miracles into two types: those that prevent customary events and those that affirm non-customary events. Through examples like the wandering of the Israelites and the confinement of Zechariah's speech, he illustrates how these miracles serve as proof. The discussion also touches on the controversial opinion that the inimitability of the Quran is a preventive miracle.

Guided Path

The author gives examples for both preventive (e.g., preventing voluntary movements, stopping sorcerers' illusions) and affirmative (e.g., the Israelites' wandering, Zechariah's speech confinement). Ask yourself why these fit each category.

The author emphasizes that the miracle is connected to the prophet's challenge. This connection ensures that the miracle serves as contextual evidence.

This passage presents a third argument: the evidence of truthfulness is inseparable from the challenge (tahaddi) of the true prophet. The author classifies miracles into two types: (1) prevention of the customary (man' al-mu'tad), such as preventing voluntary movements or stopping sorcerers' illusions, and (2) affirmation of the non-customary (ithbat ghayr al-mu'tad), which occurs within the course of custom. The Miracle Must Signify Truth
Proof that a miracle must indicate truth, with analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a miracle, as a sign from God, cannot be an indicator of falsehood, and how this reasoning is supported by analogy.

Core Idea
One sign cannot prove both truth and falsehood—it must be consistent.

The author presents a concise logical argument that a miracle, as a divine sign, must indicate the truthfulness of the prophet. If it could also indicate falsehood, it would lead to a contradiction. He then strengthens this with a simple analogy from the way existence and precision point to power and knowledge, respectively.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the compact logical flow.
The passage is only a few lines but packs a full argument.
2
Understand the core argument
Identify the claim: a miracle (āyah) is a sign of the prophet's truth. If he were a liar, the same sign would indicate falsehood—a contradiction. Therefore, it must indicate truth.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Examine the analogy
The author compares the sign of truth to how existence (wuqū‘) indicates power (qudrah) and not incapacity, and precision (iḥkām) indicates knowledge (‘ilm) and not ignorance. See how this parallel strengthens the main argument.
4
Reflect on the superiority claim
The author says this method is better than the first (previous proof). Consider why a clear logical contradiction might be stronger than other proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدعوة بالآية حتى تكون الآية دالة على صدق حالته ودرجته عند الله تعالى، وإذا قدر كونه كاذبا انقلبت الدلالة على الصدق دلالة على الكذب، وهو محال لتناقضه، وكما أن الوقوع إذا دل على القدرة لم يدل على العجز والإحكام لما دل على العلم لم يدل على الجهل ، كذلك دليل الصدق لا يجوز أن يكون دليلا على الكذب، وهذه الطريقة أحسن من الأولى.
The call with the sign (āyah) so that the sign indicates the truth of his state and his rank with God Almighty. If it were possible that he be a liar, the indication of truth would turn into an indication of falsehood, which is impossible due to contradiction. Just as occurrence (wuqū‘) when it indicates power (qudrah) does not indicate incapacity, and precision (iḥkām) when it indicates knowledge (‘ilm) does not indicate ignorance, likewise the proof of truth (dalīl al-ṣidq) cannot be a proof of falsehood (kidhb). And this method is better than the first.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is a proof (dalīl) that the miracle (āyah) must indicate truth. The author argues: The miracle is presented as a sign of the prophet's truthfulness. If the prophet were a liar, the same miracle would then indicate falsehood, which is a contradiction. So the miracle must indicate truth. He supports this with an analogy: just as existence (wujūd) indicates power (qudrah) and not incapacity, and precision (iḥkām) indicates knowledge (‘ilm) and not ignorance, similarly a sign of truth cannot be a sign of falsehood. The author then remarks that this method (ṭarīqah) is better than the first (which was likely presented earlier).

وقوع (wuqū‘)

إحكام (iḥkām)
علم (‘ilm)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think a miracle could be performed by both a true and a false prophet, and thus it does not necessarily indicate truth.
Correction: The author argues that if a miracle were performed by a liar, it would then indicate falsehood, but the same sign cannot indicate both truth and falsehood without contradiction. Therefore, a miracle must indicate truth.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
A miracle, as a divine sign, must indicate the truth of the prophet because the same sign cannot logically indicate both truth and falsehood.

Miracles: Prevention of the Customary
Classification of miracles into two types with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of miracles into two types and the concept of prevention of the customary (man' al-mu'tad) with examples from prophetic history.

Core Idea
Miracles either prevent the customary or establish the non-customary.

In this passage, the author presents a new way of proving prophethood through the continuous miracle. He begins by dividing miracles into two types: prevention of the customary and establishment of the non-customary. He provides examples such as the wandering of the Israelites and the silencing of Zachariah. This lesson focuses on the first type and the possibility of Allah preventing people from challenging the prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of miracles
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to understand the two types: prevention of the customary and establishment of the non-customary.
Notice the examples given for the first type.
2
Identify the examples
List the three examples: wandering of Israelites, prevention of sorcerers, confinement of Zachariah. Reflect on how each prevents normal custom.
3
Understand the possibility of prevention
The author says it is possible that motivations are diverted so that no one opposes. Note the reference to i'jaz al-Qur'an as a deserted opinion.
This sets up the continuous miracle argument.
4
Reflect on the classification
Consider why this classification is important for the proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه آخر نقول : إن قرينة الصدق ملازمة لتحدي النبي الصادق عن الله تعالى، وذلك أن المعجزة تنقسم إلى منع المعتاد وإلى إثبات غير المعتاد، أما المنع فكالجنس من الحركات الاختيارية مع سلامة البنية وإحساس التيسير، والثاني في مجرى العادة، ومثال ذلك: تيه بني إسرائيل في قطع الطريق، ومنع السحرة من التخييل، وحصر زكريا من الكلام المعتاد ويجوز أن يقدر صرف الدواعي عن المعارضة بمثل ما جاء به النبي عليه السلام من جنس المعجزات، وإن كان ذلك من قبيل مقدوراتهم. ولهذا عد بعضهم إعجاز القرآن من هذا القبيل وهو مذهب مهجور ويجوز أن يقدر منع الناس عن التحدي بمثل ما تحدى به النبي من جنس المعجزات، فلا أحد على المعارضة بالدعوى ، فضلا عن معارضته بالخارق للعادة، وتكون لهذه المعجزة قرينة متصلة بنفس الدعوى حتى لا تخلو قط دعوى نبي من الأنبياء عن قرينة الصدق، ولا تتأخر الدلالة عن نفس التحدي، وهذا أبلغ في باب الإعجاز، فإن المتصدي للمعارضة يحس من نفسه عجزاً مع استمرار عادته بمثل ذلك التحدي، فيقول النبي : إني لرسول الله إليكم وآية صدقي أن لا يعارضني معارض في نفس دعواي هذه والنفوس متطلعة، والألسن سليمة، والدواعي باعثة، فتتحير العقول وتنحصر الألسن، وتتراجع الدواعي، وتنمحق الدعاوي، لست أقول : لا ينكره منكر، بل أقول لا يعارضه معارض بمثل التحدي والدعوى، فيقول : لا ، بل إني رسول الله إليكم. ولهذا لم نجد في قصص الأنبياء من عارضهم بمثل دعواهم في حال التحدي، ولا استمرت هذه الدعوى لأحد من بعدهم ولا يلتفت إلى ما يحكى عن مسيلمة الكذاب أنه ادعى الرسالة عن الله تعالى فإن من كتب إلى نبي الله تعالى: أما بعد فإن الأرض بيني وبينك نصفين لم يكن معارضاً له في نفس دعواه، بل مسلما له من وجه ومتحكما من وجه، ومن ادعى الرحمانية في الحالة الثانية لم يكن ثابت القدم على الدعوى الأولة، وكان من حقه لو كان متنازعا له أن يقول : إني عبد
Another way: We say: Indeed, the concomitant of truth (qarīnat al-ṣidq) is inseparable from the challenge of the truthful prophet from God Almighty. That is because the miracle (mu‘jizah) is divided into prevention of the customary (man‘ al-mu‘tād) and establishment of the non-customary (ithbāt ghayr al-mu‘tād). As for prevention, it is like the genus of voluntary movements with sound constitution and the feeling of facilitation; the second is in the course of custom. An example of that: the wandering of the Children of Israel in crossing the road, the prevention of the sorcerers from illusion, and the confinement of Zachariah from customary speech. And it is possible that the motivations be diverted from opposing with something like what the prophet, peace be upon him, brought of the genus of miracles, even if that is of the realm of their capabilities. For this reason, some have counted the inimitability of the Qur’an (i‘jāz al-Qur’ān) as being of this kind—a deserted opinion. And it is possible that people are prevented from challenging with something like what the prophet challenged with of the genus of miracles, so no one engages in opposition with the claim, let alone opposing him with the miraculous. And this miracle has a continuous concomitant (qarīnah muttaṣilah) to the claim itself, so that never does any prophet’s claim lack a concomitant of truth, nor does the indication lag behind the challenge itself. And this is more emphatic in the matter of inimitability. For the one who sets out to oppose feels from himself incapacity while his custom continues with such a challenge. So the prophet says: ‘I am the messenger of God to you, and the sign of my truth is that no opponent opposes me in this very claim of mine—while souls are eager, tongues are free, and motivations are inciting.’ So minds become bewildered, tongues are confined, motivations recede, and claims are obliterated. I do not say that no denier denies him, rather I say that no opponent opposes him with a similar challenge and claim. So he says: ‘No, rather I am the messenger of God to you.’ For this reason, we do not find in the stories of the prophets anyone who opposed them with a similar claim during the state of challenge, nor did this claim persist for anyone after them. And no attention is paid to what is narrated about Musaylimah the Liar that he claimed prophethood from God Almighty, for he who wrote to the Prophet of God: ‘To proceed, indeed the land is between me and you halves’—he was not an opponent to him in the very claim; rather, he was acknowledging him in one respect and domineering in another. And whoever claimed divinity (raḥmāniyyah) in the second state was not firm-footed on the first claim, and it would have been required of him—if he were a contender—to say: ‘I am a servant.’
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage presents another argument (wajh ākhar) based on the continuous miracle (qarīnah muttaṣilah). The author first classifies miracles into two types: (1) prevention of the customary (man‘ al-mu‘tād) — for example, the Israelites going astray, the magicians being prevented from their sorcery, and Zakariya being prevented from speech; and (2) establishing the non-customary (ithbāt ghayr al-mu‘tād). He notes that some scholars consider the inimitability of the Qur’an to be of the first type, but that view is abandoned (madhhab mahjūr). He then explains that it is possible that people are prevented from challenging the prophet with a similar miracle, so no one can oppose the claim, let alone produce a counter-miracle. Thus the miracle becomes a continuous concomitant (qarīnah muttaṣilah) of the claim itself, never separated from it. The challenge is that the prophet says, 'I am the messenger of God to you, and the sign of my truth is that no one will oppose me in this very claim, while souls are eager, tongues are free, and motivations are present.' As a result, minds are bewildered, tongues are silenced, motivations recede, and claims vanish. The author clarifies that he does not mean no one will deny the prophet, but rather no one will oppose with a similar claim and challenge. This is why in the stories of the prophets we never find anyone opposing them with a similar claim during their challenge, nor did this claim continue after them. He then refutes the story of Musaylima the Liar, who wrote to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) saying 'the earth is half for me and half for you.' This was not an opposition to the claim itself, but rather an acknowledgment from one angle and an overbearing from another. Moreover, anyone who later claimed divinity (raḥmāniyyah) was not established in the first claim, and would have been required to say 'I am the servant of God' if he were truly a contender.

Key Terms
قرينة الصدق (qarīnat al-ṣidq)
تحدي (taḥaddī)
معجزة (mu‘jizah)
منع المعتاد (man‘ al-mu‘tād)
إثبات غير المعتاد (ithbāt ghayr al-mu‘tād)
إعجاز القرآن (i‘jāz al-Qur’ān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divided into prevention of the customary and establishment of the non-customary; the prevention type involves Allah stopping normal events to prove the prophet's truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Continuous Miracle and Refutation of Musaylima
Explanation of continuous miracle and refutation of Musaylima.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the continuous miracle (qarīnah muttaṣilah) functions as an inseparable proof of prophethood and how the author refutes the example of Musaylima.

Core Idea
The continuous miracle prevents anyone from opposing the prophet's claim with a similar challenge.

In this part of the passage, the author explains that the miracle is a continuous concomitant (qarīnah muttaṣilah) that never separates from the prophet's claim. He describes the effect on those who would oppose: they feel incapable despite having all motivations. He then addresses the story of Musaylima the Liar, showing that his letter was not a genuine opposition.

Guided Path
1
Read the continuous miracle argument
Focus on how the miracle becomes a continuous concomitant that never leaves the prophet's claim.
2
Visualize the challenge scenario
Imagine the prophet making his claim and the would-be opponent feeling incapable despite having all means.
The author describes minds bewildered and tongues confined.
3
Understand the clarification
Note that the author distinguishes between denial (which may happen) and opposition with a similar claim (which does not happen).
4
Analyze the refutation of Musaylima
Read the author's response to Musaylima's letter. Why is it not a genuine opposition?
The key is that Musaylima acknowledged the Prophet in some way.

ووجه آخر نقول : إن قرينة الصدق ملازمة لتحدي النبي الصادق عن الله تعالى، وذلك أن المعجزة تنقسم إلى منع المعتاد وإلى إثبات غير المعتاد، أما المنع فكالجنس من الحركات الاختيارية مع سلامة البنية وإحساس التيسير، والثاني في مجرى العادة، ومثال ذلك: تيه بني إسرائيل في قطع الطريق، ومنع السحرة من التخييل، وحصر زكريا من الكلام المعتاد ويجوز أن يقدر صرف الدواعي عن المعارضة بمثل ما جاء به النبي عليه السلام من جنس المعجزات، وإن كان ذلك من قبيل مقدوراتهم. ولهذا عد بعضهم إعجاز القرآن من هذا القبيل وهو مذهب مهجور ويجوز أن يقدر منع الناس عن التحدي بمثل ما تحدى به النبي من جنس المعجزات، فلا أحد على المعارضة بالدعوى ، فضلا عن معارضته بالخارق للعادة، وتكون لهذه المعجزة قرينة متصلة بنفس الدعوى حتى لا تخلو قط دعوى نبي من الأنبياء عن قرينة الصدق، ولا تتأخر الدلالة عن نفس التحدي، وهذا أبلغ في باب الإعجاز، فإن المتصدي للمعارضة يحس من نفسه عجزاً مع استمرار عادته بمثل ذلك التحدي، فيقول النبي : إني لرسول الله إليكم وآية صدقي أن لا يعارضني معارض في نفس دعواي هذه والنفوس متطلعة، والألسن سليمة، والدواعي باعثة، فتتحير العقول وتنحصر الألسن، وتتراجع الدواعي، وتنمحق الدعاوي، لست أقول : لا ينكره منكر، بل أقول لا يعارضه معارض بمثل التحدي والدعوى، فيقول : لا ، بل إني رسول الله إليكم. ولهذا لم نجد في قصص الأنبياء من عارضهم بمثل دعواهم في حال التحدي، ولا استمرت هذه الدعوى لأحد من بعدهم ولا يلتفت إلى ما يحكى عن مسيلمة الكذاب أنه ادعى الرسالة عن الله تعالى فإن من كتب إلى نبي الله تعالى: أما بعد فإن الأرض بيني وبينك نصفين لم يكن معارضاً له في نفس دعواه، بل مسلما له من وجه ومتحكما من وجه، ومن ادعى الرحمانية في الحالة الثانية لم يكن ثابت القدم على الدعوى الأولة، وكان من حقه لو كان متنازعا له أن يقول : إني عبد
Another way: We say: Indeed, the concomitant of truth (qarīnat al-ṣidq) is inseparable from the challenge of the truthful prophet from God Almighty. That is because the miracle (mu‘jizah) is divided into prevention of the customary (man‘ al-mu‘tād) and establishment of the non-customary (ithbāt ghayr al-mu‘tād). As for prevention, it is like the genus of voluntary movements with sound constitution and the feeling of facilitation; the second is in the course of custom. An example of that: the wandering of the Children of Israel in crossing the road, the prevention of the sorcerers from illusion, and the confinement of Zachariah from customary speech. And it is possible that the motivations be diverted from opposing with something like what the prophet, peace be upon him, brought of the genus of miracles, even if that is of the realm of their capabilities. For this reason, some have counted the inimitability of the Qur’an (i‘jāz al-Qur’ān) as being of this kind—a deserted opinion. And it is possible that people are prevented from challenging with something like what the prophet challenged with of the genus of miracles, so no one engages in opposition with the claim, let alone opposing him with the miraculous. And this miracle has a continuous concomitant (qarīnah muttaṣilah) to the claim itself, so that never does any prophet’s claim lack a concomitant of truth, nor does the indication lag behind the challenge itself. And this is more emphatic in the matter of inimitability. For the one who sets out to oppose feels from himself incapacity while his custom continues with such a challenge. So the prophet says: ‘I am the messenger of God to you, and the sign of my truth is that no opponent opposes me in this very claim of mine—while souls are eager, tongues are free, and motivations are inciting.’ So minds become bewildered, tongues are confined, motivations recede, and claims are obliterated. I do not say that no denier denies him, rather I say that no opponent opposes him with a similar challenge and claim. So he says: ‘No, rather I am the messenger of God to you.’ For this reason, we do not find in the stories of the prophets anyone who opposed them with a similar claim during the state of challenge, nor did this claim persist for anyone after them. And no attention is paid to what is narrated about Musaylimah the Liar that he claimed prophethood from God Almighty, for he who wrote to the Prophet of God: ‘To proceed, indeed the land is between me and you halves’—he was not an opponent to him in the very claim; rather, he was acknowledging him in one respect and domineering in another. And whoever claimed divinity (raḥmāniyyah) in the second state was not firm-footed on the first claim, and it would have been required of him—if he were a contender—to say: ‘I am a servant.’
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage presents another argument (wajh ākhar) based on the continuous miracle (qarīnah muttaṣilah). The author first classifies miracles into two types: (1) prevention of the customary (man‘ al-mu‘tād) — for example, the Israelites going astray, the magicians being prevented from their sorcery, and Zakariya being prevented from speech; and (2) establishing the non-customary (ithbāt ghayr al-mu‘tād). He notes that some scholars consider the inimitability of the Qur’an to be of the first type, but that view is abandoned (madhhab mahjūr). He then explains that it is possible that people are prevented from challenging the prophet with a similar miracle, so no one can oppose the claim, let alone produce a counter-miracle. Thus the miracle becomes a continuous concomitant (qarīnah muttaṣilah) of the claim itself, never separated from it. The challenge is that the prophet says, 'I am the messenger of God to you, and the sign of my truth is that no one will oppose me in this very claim, while souls are eager, tongues are free, and motivations are present.' As a result, minds are bewildered, tongues are silenced, motivations recede, and claims vanish. The author clarifies that he does not mean no one will deny the prophet, but rather no one will oppose with a similar claim and challenge. This is why in the stories of the prophets we never find anyone opposing them with a similar claim during their challenge, nor did this claim continue after them. He then refutes the story of Musaylima the Liar, who wrote to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) saying 'the earth is half for me and half for you.' This was not an opposition to the claim itself, but rather an acknowledgment from one angle and an overbearing from another. Moreover, anyone who later claimed divinity (raḥmāniyyah) was not established in the first claim, and would have been required to say 'I am the servant of God' if he were truly a contender.

Key Terms
قرينة الصدق (qarīnat al-ṣidq)
قرينة متصلة (qarīnah muttaṣilah)
تحدي (taḥaddī)
معجزة (mu‘jizah)
مسيلمة الكذاب (Musaylimah al-Kadhdhāb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Musaylima's claim was a genuine counter-challenge to Prophet Muhammad.
Correction: The author explains that Musaylima's letter was not an opposition to the same claim; it acknowledged the Prophet in one respect and demanded power-sharing, not a claim to prophethood in the same sense.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what happens to the one who sets out to oppose the prophet?
A) He feels incapable
B) He becomes a prophet
C) He denies him
D) He succeeds

Key Takeaway
The continuous miracle ensures that no one can oppose the prophet's claim with a similar challenge, and historical examples confirm this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the continuous miracle leaves no room for a rival claimant. But what about the claims of your own ego? Have you ever, in your heart, set yourself up as a rival to Allah's command, thinking you know better? What would it mean for you to truly accept that no one can challenge Allah's messenger? Will you surrender that last bit of pride today?
?
The author says that the opponent feels incapacity while his custom continues. Are there areas in your life where you persist in opposing Allah's guidance, even though deep down you know you cannot match it? What is holding you back from admitting your helplessness and submitting?
?
Musaylima acknowledged the Prophet in one respect but was domineering in another. Is there a part of your faith where you acknowledge Allah but then act as if you are in control? Where do you need to stop dividing the 'land' and instead say 'I am a servant'?

The Impossible Challenge: No One Opposes a True Prophet
Author proves no one successfully opposed a prophet's challenge, citing Musaylimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the impossibility of successful opposition to a prophet's challenge serves as a proof of prophethood, and why the case of Musaylimah is not a counterexample.

Core Idea
No one can successfully match a prophet's challenge—proof of their truth.

This passage from al-‘Aqida al-Tahawiyya explains one of the key signs of prophethood: the challenge (tahaddi). When a true prophet issues a challenge, no one can successfully oppose it. This lesson unpacks the argument and clarifies the famous case of Musaylimah.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the full argument.
2
Identify the main claim
Notice that the author distinguishes between denial and opposition. The prophet's sign is that no one can oppose with a similar claim.
This is a subtle but crucial distinction.
3
Analyze the Musaylimah objection
See how the author refutes the apparent counterexample of Musaylimah by showing he implicitly accepted the Prophet's claim.
The letter addressed 'to the Prophet of God'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبياء عن قرينة الصدق، ولا تتأخر الدلالة عن نفس التحدي، وهذا أبلغ في باب الإعجاز، فإن المتصدي للمعارضة يحس من نفسه عجزاً مع استمرار عادته بمثل ذلك التحدي، فيقول النبي : إني لرسول الله إليكم وآية صدقي أن لا يعارضني معارض في نفس دعواي هذه والنفوس متطلعة، والألسن سليمة، والدواعي باعثة، فتتحير العقول وتنحصر الألسن، وتتراجع الدواعي، وتنمحق الدعاوي، لست أقول : لا ينكره منكر، بل أقول لا يعارضه معارض بمثل التحدي والدعوى، فيقول : لا، بل إني رسول الله إليكم. ولهذا لم نجد في قصص الأنبياء من عارضهم بمثل دعواهم في حال التحدي، ولا استمرت هذه الدعوى لأحد من بعدهم ولا يلتفت إلى ما يحكى عن مسيلمة الكذاب أنه ادعى الرسالة عن الله تعالى فإن من كتب إلى نبي الله تعالى، فإن من كتب إلى نبي الله : أما بعد فإن الأرض بيني وبينك نصفين لم يكن معارضاً له في نفس دعواه، بل مسلما له من وجه ومتحكما من وجه، ومن ادعى الرحمانية في الحالة الثانية لم يكن ثابت القدم على الدعوى الأولة، وكان من حقه لو كان متنازعا له أن يقول : إني عبد الله ونبيه لا شريك الله في الرحمانية وشريك رسوله في الأرض، فاعرف هذه الدقيقة فإن فيها سراً وغوراً.
The prophets concerning the indication of truthfulness, and the indication is not delayed from the challenge itself, and this is more powerful in the chapter of inimitability, for the one who sets out to oppose feels from himself incapacity despite the continuity of his habit with such a challenge, so the prophet says: I am the messenger of God to you, and the sign of my truthfulness is that no opponent will oppose me in this very claim of mine while souls are eager, tongues are fluent, and motives are impelling, so minds become perplexed, tongues are restrained, motives retreat, and claims are obliterated. I do not say: no denier denies it, but I say: no opponent opposes it with a similar challenge and claim, and he says: No, rather I am the messenger of God to you. And for this reason we do not find in the stories of the prophets anyone who opposed them with a similar claim during the state of challenge, nor did this claim continue for anyone after them, and no attention is paid to what is related about Musaylimah the liar that he claimed prophethood from God Almighty, for he who wrote to the Prophet of God: 'As for what follows, the land is between me and you in halves' was not an opposer to him in his very claim, but rather a submitter to him in one respect and an authority-seeker in another respect. And whoever claimed divinity in the second state was not firm of foot on the first claim, and it would have been his right, if he were a contender, to say: I am the servant of God and His prophet, not a partner of God in divinity nor a partner of His messenger on earth. Know this subtlety, for it contains a secret and depth.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an argument proving the truthfulness of prophets through the impossibility of successful opposition during a challenge. The author begins by stating that the miracle is an immediate indication of truth, not delayed, which is the strongest form of inimitability. When a prophet issues a challenge, the would-be opponent feels inherent incapacity despite his usual ability. The prophet declares that no one will oppose him successfully in that very claim, and indeed, minds become perplexed, tongues restrained, and motives retreat. The author clarifies that he does not mean no one denies the claim—rather, no one successfully opposes it with a similar challenge. He then gives the historical evidence: in all prophetic stories, no one ever successfully opposed a prophet during a challenge. He addresses the case of Musaylimah, who wrote to the Prophet Muhammad proposing to divide the land. The author argues that Musaylimah was not truly opposing the Prophet's claim; by addressing him as a prophet (writing to 'the Prophet of God'), he effectively acknowledged Muhammad's prophethood. Moreover, Musaylimah's later claim to divinity contradicted his earlier implicit admission, showing inconsistency. The author concludes by urging the reader to grasp this subtle point, which contains deep insight.

Key Terms
التحدي
المعارضة
المعجزة
مسيلمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Musaylimah successfully opposed the Prophet's challenge and claimed prophethood, disproving the sign.
Correction: Musaylimah implicitly accepted Muhammad's prophethood by addressing him as 'the Prophet of God'; thus he did not truly oppose the challenge. His later claim to divinity was inconsistent with his earlier admission.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider Musaylimah's letter not a true opposition to Prophet Muhammad's claim?
A) Because Musaylimah was insane and incapable of reasoning.
B) Because Musaylimah addressed Muhammad as 'the Prophet of God', thereby acknowledging his prophethood.
C) Because Musaylimah did not explicitly deny Muhammad's prophethood.
D) Because Musaylimah proposed a division of land, which is unrelated to prophethood.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of successful opposition to a prophet's challenge is a key sign of truth, and historical counterexamples like Musaylimah actually confirm the sign when properly understood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that no one could successfully oppose the Prophet's claim. If you truly believe this, why do you still allow your doubts and desires to oppose the Prophet's commands in your daily life? What one command will you commit to obeying fully from today?
?
The author says the opponent feels incapacity despite having eager souls and fluent tongues. Have you ever felt that incapacity when faced with the truth of Islam—perhaps when you tried to argue against a teaching but found your arguments falling short? What did you do with that feeling? Will you now submit to that truth?
?
Musaylimah half-submitted and half-claimed authority. Are there areas of your life where you acknowledge Allah's sovereignty with your lips but act as if you are in control—like your finances, relationships, or future plans? What is one practical step you can take today to surrender that area entirely to Allah?
